      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Niuean_language" title="Niuean language">Niuean</a> (official) 46% (a <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Polynesian language">Polynesian language</a> closely related to <a href="/wiki/Tongan_language" title="Tongan language">Tongan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samoan_language" title="Samoan language">Samoan</a>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Niuean_language" title="Niuean language">Niuean</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> 32%</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> (official) 11%</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Niuean_language" title="Niuean language">Niuean</a> and others 5%,</li> 
       <li>Other 6%</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Niue" title="Music of Niue">Music of Niue</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Niuean_dancing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Niuean_dancing.jpg/220px-Niuean_dancing.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Niuean_dancing.jpg/330px-Niuean_dancing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Niuean_dancing.jpg/440px-Niuean_dancing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2564" data-file-height="1668"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Niuean_dancing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Niuean dancers at the <a href="/wiki/Pasifika_Festival" title="Pasifika Festival">Pasifika Festival</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Niue is the birthplace of New Zealand artist and writer <a href="/wiki/John_Pule" title="John Pule">John Pule</a>. Author of <i>The Shark That Ate the Sun</i>, he also paints <a href="/wiki/Tapa_cloth" title="Tapa cloth">tapa cloth</a> inspired designs on canvas.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> In 2005, he co-wrote <i>Hiapo: Past and Present in Niuean Barkcloth</i>, a study of a traditional Niuean artform, with Australian writer and anthropologist Nicholas Thomas.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Taoga_Niue" title="Taoga Niue">Taoga Niue</a> is a new Government Department responsible for the preservation of culture, tradition and heritage. Recognising its importance, the Government has added Taoga Niue as the sixth pillar of the <a href="/wiki/Niue_Integrated_Strategic_Plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Niue Integrated Strategic Plan">Niue Integrated Strategic Plan</a> (NISP). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Niue has two broadcast outlets, <a href="/wiki/Television_Niue" class="mw-redirect" title="Television Niue">Television Niue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radio_Sunshine" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio Sunshine">Radio Sunshine</a>, managed and operated by the <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_Corporation_of_Niue" title="Broadcasting Corporation of Niue">Broadcasting Corporation of Niue</a>, and one newspaper, the <i><a href="/wiki/Niue_Star" title="Niue Star">Niue Star</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Niue" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby union in Niue">Rugby union in Niue</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Niuean_haka.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Niuean_haka.jpg/220px-Niuean_haka.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Niuean_haka.jpg/330px-Niuean_haka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Niuean_haka.jpg/440px-Niuean_haka.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Niuean_haka.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Niue sevens team performing a <a href="/wiki/Takalo" title="Takalo">takalo</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Despite being a small country, a number of sports are popular. <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a> is the most popular sport, played by both men and women; Niue was the 2008 <a href="/wiki/FORU_Oceania_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="FORU Oceania Cup">FORU Oceania Cup</a> champions.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">Netball</a> is played only by women. There is a nine-hole <a href="/wiki/Golf_course" title="Golf course">golf course</a> at Fonuakula. There is a lawn <a href="/wiki/Bowling_green" title="Bowling green">bowling green</a> under construction.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Association Football is a popular sport, as evidenced by the <a href="/wiki/Niue_Soccer_Tournament" title="Niue Soccer Tournament">Niue Soccer Tournament</a>, though the <a href="/wiki/Niue_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Niue national football team">Niue national football team</a> has played only <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1983_South_Pacific_Games#Group_B" title="Football at the 1983 South Pacific Games">two matches</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">Rugby league</a> is also a popular sport. Niue Rugby League have only started making strides within the international arena since their first ever test match against Vanuatu, going down 22–20 in 2013. On 4 October 2014, the Niue rugby league team record their first ever international test match win defeating the Philippines 36–22. In May 2015, Niue Rugby League recorded their second international test match win against the South African Rugby League side, 48–4. Niue now sit 31st in the Rugby League World Rankings. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright">

        <li><span><a href="/wiki/File:%E5%A4%A7%E6%B4%8B.png" class="image"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%E5%A4%A7%E6%B4%8B.png/32px-%E5%A4%A7%E6%B4%8B.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="26" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%E5%A4%A7%E6%B4%8B.png/48px-%E5%A4%A7%E6%B4%8B.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%E5%A4%A7%E6%B4%8B.png/64px-%E5%A4%A7%E6%B4%8B.png 2x" data-file-width="756" data-file-height="617"></a></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Oceania" title="Portal:Oceania">Oceania portal</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <ul>
       <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.theguardian.com/world/2014/jul/13/niue-pacific-island-struggling-population-new-zealand#comment-38104481">Niue, the Pacific island struggling to cope as its population plummets</a></li> 
       <li>Chapman, Terry M. (1976) – <i>The Decolonisation of Niue.</i></li> 
       <li>Hekau, Maihetoe &amp; al., <i>Niue: A History of the Island</i>, <a href="/wiki/Suva" title="Suva">Suva</a>: Institute of Pacific Studies (<a href="/wiki/University_of_the_South_Pacific" title="University of the South Pacific">USP</a>) &amp; the government of Niue, 1982 [no ISBN]</li> 
       <li>Loeb, Edwin M. (1926) – <i>History and Traditions of Niue.</i></li> 
       <li>Painter, Margaret and Kalaisi Folau (2000) – <i>Tagi Tote e Loto Haaku, My Heart Is Crying a Little: Niue Island Involvement in the Great War, 1914–1918.</i></li> 
       <li>Smith, Percy – <i>Niue-fekai (or Savage) Island and its People.</i></li> 
       <li>Sperlich, Wolfgang B. (2012) – <i>Tohi Vagahau Niue/Niue Language Dictionary: Niuean-English, with English-Niuean Finderlist.</i></li> 
       <li>Thomson, Basil C. (2012) – <i>Savage Island: An Account of a Sojourn in Niue and Tonga.</i></li> 
       <li>James P Terry and Warwick E Murray (edited by) - <i>Niue Island: Geographical Perspectives on the Rock of Polynesia</i> International Scientific Council for Island Development (INSULA), UNESCO, 
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9299002304" title="Special:BookSources/9299002304">9299002304</a>.</li> 
       <li>SPREP, Rod Hay and Ralph Powlesland, Compiled by Joanna Sim –<i>Guide to Birds of Niue</i></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Edward_Tregear" title="Edward Tregear">Tregear, Edward</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jps.auckland.ac.nz/document/Volume_2_1893/Volume_2%2C_No.1%2C_March_1893/Niue%3A_or_Savage_Island%2C_by_Edward_Tregear%2C_p_11-16/p1?action=null">"Niue: or Savage Island"</a>, <i>The Journal of the <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_Society" title="Polynesian Society">Polynesian Society</a></i>, vol.2, March 1893, pp.&nbsp;11–16</li> 
       <li>W R Sykes – <i>Contributions to the Flora of Niue</i></li> 
       <li>Dick Scott (1993) – <i>Would a Good Man Die</i></li>
      </ul>

                      <ul>
                       <li>1.&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Condominium_(international_law)" title="Condominium (international law)">Occupied jointly</a> with the United States.</li> 
                       <li>2.&nbsp;In 1931, Canada and other British <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">dominions</a> obtained self-government through the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster</a>. See <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Canada" title="Name of Canada">Name of Canada</a>.</li> 
                       <li>3.&nbsp;Gave up <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">self-rule</a> in 1934, but remained a <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> Dominion until it <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">joined Canada</a> in 1949.</li>
                      </ul>
